  40. I love the [[ASIN:B00CUG270S Philips Sonicare HX8211/02 Airfloss Rechargeable Electric Flosser]] and have been using it twice a day since it arrived and was fully charged. I use either water or a combination of water and mouthwash to get between each and every tooth in my mouth, focusing on the areas where I have gold crowns that trap more food than I can believe. Since I received this electric flosser, I haven't needed to use the toothpicks I'd gotten into the habit of picking with each night after dinner. I simply fill the reservoir, prime the pump, then proceed. By keeping the mouth closed, liquid remains in the mouth and I've yet to experience dripping or squirting anywhere. I use either the automatic repeat action or take my time and press the activating button as I insert the tip between the teeth. Snapping the tip at first required more force than I'd anticipated, but I've learned that it really must be snug to work properly, so when I remove it for cleaning, I double check to be sure it's firmly seated in the base. This has been holding a charge for me, but I must add that I really do like to keep it on the base plugged into an outlet, as I've been doing with my Sonicare electric toothbrush for many years. This device is not intended to take the place of your flossing, it's a tool to stimulate the gums using water and force, forcing particles free of the teeth trap. Together, your dental hygiene will be improved and your digestion will also thank you for keeping the first step of that process in good condition.

I haven't tried it yet, but according to some reviewers, it DOES do at least as good a job as traditional flossing.<br /><br />I'll conclude with a final word for people who are not flossing regularly: One way to encourage yourself to floss at least once daily is to use colored floss (Johnson and Johnson Reach makes a waxed mint floss that's green in color). Colored floss helps you see plaque build-up much better than floss that's colored white. Once you see the plaque that comes off between your teeth every day, you will WANT to floss every day!<br /><br />---<br />The Verdict On The Philips Sonicare Airfloss Electric Flosser: Recommended with reservations.

  53. I suffer from the kind of terminal laziness that most of us non-flossers have, and this product has been a wonderful solution. I use water rather than mouthwash, preferring to swish some mouthwash around following flossing, and I have noticed a significant change in my overall oral sensitivity and the infrequent bleeding I used to experience when flossing has gone away completely. Although it is a little messy at first, at the worst it resulted in drops on the counter and mirror, and I have since learned to use it with very minimal splash back. The reservoir holds more than enough water for my entire mouth and I have had zero issues with the function of the product after daily use for several weeks. Many people complain about how this is not as good as using string floss, and I would agree that if you have a particle of food stuck between your teeth above the gum line, using regular floss to remove it might be a better solution, but this product is absolutely perfect for me and has made a huge difference already, despite having only been used for a short time. I have several close-set and overlapping teeth, but have found it to work even in those instances. I think the greatest benefit for me, however, has been that the simplicity has allowed me, despite my resistance to flossing, to get into a positive routine. Sure, you might say I should have just bucked up and been responsible about flossing in the first place, and that's true, but this product has been more pleasant and significantly easier than anything else I've tried and has made me a daily flosser. I definitely recommend this to anyone with oral sensitivity, and those who do not regularly floss.

  148. This &#34;Electric Flosser&#34; is a modern twist on the old &#34;Waterpics&#34; you might remember from the 70's and 80s. The difference is that on this one the water reservoir is in the handle, and instead of constant pulses of water, this one puts out individual pulses about a second apart. You move it from tooth to tooth between blasts.<br /><br />This does have some advantages over the old Waterpics. One is, that since individual blasts are sent once a second, you can position the device, and then receive the single blast of water right between your teeth. As such, there is much less water dribbling out of your mouth, or getting sprayed everywhere, which was my experience with the older devices.<br /><br />So, the product pretty much works as advertised, and will deliver a sharp burst of water right between your teeth to help clean between your teeth.<br /><br />It works as advertised, but is it a product I will use . . . probably not. It is one more thing to keep plugged in on your bathroom countertop, and I really do not see the true benefit of the device. If you are someone who already flosses your teeth, you will not like this device because it simply can not do the job that flossing does. No way will a burst of water clean like the physical &#34;scraping&#34; you get with floss. Second, if you are someone who does not take the time to floss, you will probably not take the time to use this device. I can floss my teeth just as quickly as it takes to get between all the teeth with this device.<br /><br />Bottom line is I really like sonicare products, and in general believe they make good stuff, but unfortunately I think that this particular device is ill-conceived and probably is not going to be used by many people.

  191. The biggest \\"flaw\\" in this product is that it calls itself a \\"flosser\\" which invites comparison to the outcome you experience when you use conventional floss. This does perform some of the functions of floss, some that it does not, and doesn't do some that it does. The main difference is that floss will help remove large bits of food (liked trapped bits of popcorn or chicken) and the documentation on this explicitly says that it is not designed to do that.<br /><br />On the other hand, this does use a blast of air and water to push food particles from between your teeth. It likely does it in a more uniform and effective way than floss, particularly if you are not a skilled flosser. When I last went to the dentist, I was advised to be sure that I ran the floss up and down both sides of adjacent teeth (that means two passes between each tooth with the floss) and not to just pull it once between them. Most people hate flossing and do it fast and sloppy. If you're one of these people, there is a good chance that the Sonicare is going to do more for your oral hygiene than a cursory or poor flossing.<br /><br />The way I see this is as not a substitute for using floss, but as an adjunct. This works so fast that you could easily use it 2-3 times a day just before brushing and could add more \\"flossing\\" to your daily routine in this way. I think how close your teeth are will also have an impact on how it works. Mine are uneven - some are tight and some are loosely spaced. It seemed to work okay with all of them, but it's hard to know for sure without some pretty close dental examination. I can say that it did blast out bits of coarsely ground black pepper that was between my teeth. If you want to test it, be sure to spit out the water it uses rather than swallow it.<br /><br />The main drawback that I experience was that, if I held it slightly wrong, the force behind the air and water could sting my tongue a little. Also, it is messy. You're supposed to hold your mouth closed a bit to make sure you're not drooling it out everywhere, but it is virtually impossible to do this for all of your teeth. So, this is messier than flossing, though almost certainly more sanitary as long as you keep the tip clean.d a bit to make sure you're not drooling it out everywhere, but it is virtually impossible to do this for all of your teeth.   195. This is an interesting product, as electric toothbrushes have been around for a while, but an electric flosser is pretty new. You have to charge it for 24 hrs before first use, and wait for the indicator light to turn green. A fully charged flosser lasts about two weeks before the next charge. If its low on charge, the light turns yellow. To fill it with water or mouthwash, you attach the nozzle, filling the reservoir, which holds enough liquid for 1 or 2 uses. To turn it on you press the power button, and press it a couple of times until it sprays well. To clean your teeth with it, you have to put the tip at the gum line between the teeth and keep moving it to direct spray between the teeth. You can either do the \\"auto-burst\\" function--which menas you hold down the activation button and the spray bursts every second, or you can choose to control the pace yourself and press the \\"single-burst\\" function to release individual bursts. This flosser can only be used on the front outside surface of the teeth.   260. Flossing is said to reduce heart attacks and grant you an extra 7 years of life. Your teeth will also look whiter if you floss since you will get into the nooks and crannies and get the dirt out.<br /><br />It's for at least those three reasons that I am an avid flosser. Often, I floss up to three times a day. I didn't always floss that frequently. In fact, until I was about 16 years old, I never flossed. Ever.<br /><br />Then I got my first oral-B Hummingbird Flosser (since discontinued), which truly taught me to appreciate how much cleaner my gums felt after flossing. I've been flossing with a variety of different devices ever since, including but not limited to all kinds of floss, dental tape, Oral-B flosser with a handle, flosser toothpicks, and the hummingbird flosser.<br /><br />I have never tried an electric flosser until I tried Sonicare. Having tried practically every electronic toothbrush on the market, I prefer Sonicare's toothbrush above all others.<br /><br />Sonicare Airfloss is nicer than flossing manually, and it's more powerful than a Hummingbird.<br /><br />But how does it work? How effective is it?<br /><br />I've used it prior to brushing my teeth and found that a lot of stuff came out. I used it after I brushed my teeth and practically nothing came out. I would then go over with a regular floss and find that in a few instances the Airflosser did not get a few food particles out.<br /><br />I like the convenience of using the Airflosser though since it's a lot faster to use than flossing by hand. The downside to that is that the Airflosser is one-directional -- you can only do it from the outside of your teeth, not inside your mouth. This means that if your teeth are really close together, are crooked, or overlap, you will not get the full benefits of flossing (i.e., getting into every nook and cranny to get every last bit of the food particles that the brush missed).<br /><br />Additionally, I also felt that the electric flosser was unnecessarily harsh. Although my gums didn't bleed (as per the warning in the instructions), they did feel sore the first few times I used the Airflosser.<br /><br />Although I never use mouthwash, I prefer to put a little bit of mouthwash into the Airflosser (the alternative is water). it leaves a much cleaner feeling and doesn't seem to make my gums as sensitive to the burst of air that the Airflosser generates.<br /><br />I think the Airflosser would be good for someone transitioning into flossing. It's a good starter tool - since it leaves the person experiencing the cleaner mouth, maybe it will lead to good hygiene and flossing technique with a regular, manual string, much like what the Hummingbird did for me years ago.For those of us who meticulous floss after every meal, the Airflosser will feel inadequate.

  265. The Philips Sonicare HX8211/02 Airfloss Rechargeable Electric Flosser is not a replacement for true flossing (with actual floss). However, it can be helpful as part of the rotation for a versatile tooth cleaning routine. For example, in situations where tooth location and dexterity issues may make it hard to get to a particular spot with traditional floss or floss picks. It can also be a \\"better than nothing\\" option on days/nights where you may be too tired or brain dead for a proper manual flossing.<br /><br />It takes a few days to get the hang of it. There are two ways to use it. Manual bursts by pressing the button up top (at the green colored incline) for each individual burst, or putting it in 1-second burst mode, where it shoots a burst every 1 second.<br /><br />You can fill the small reservoir with either water or mouth wash, your choice. I prefer water. The reservoir is not as deep as the product pictures here may indicate. It is fairly shallow.<br /><br />The battery is built-in the device, so there's only way to charge it, by using the included AC adapter. The device is not sitting solidly on the AC charging dock. It wobbles if you touch it. The instructions say to charge it for 24 hours for the first time (the first charge).<br /><br />The user manual states that this must only be used from the outer side of the teeth, not from within. It does not state why this is so.<br /><br />It is always a good idea to ask your dentist before using things like this, especially if you have work in progress or any other special situations or on-going issues and such. The water+air has some pressure to it - you may want to test it before using it in your mouth. For example, I can feel the hit on my palm a couple of inches away from the nozzle opening.<br /><br />UNBOXING: the device is inside a blister pack that is inside the outer box. The blister pack is easy to open without tools by separating the two interlocking parts. Inside the blister pack you will find the device, its AC charging dock, and paperwork (quick start guide, longer guide, registration). The registration card says if you register it, you get an additional six months added to the warranty. The base of the device and the detachable floss tip are individually wrapped for extra protection.
